(alert: "Hello! Inspired by Depression Quest by Zoë Quinn, the game you are about to play depicts one person's experience with generalized anxiety disorder. However, everyone who has anxiety has their own unique experiences, and the game's depiction is only one example. It is not representative or all-encompassing of all aspects of anxiety, its symptoms, or its outcomes. If you believe you are suffering from severe anxiety, recieving treatment from a mental health professional is highly encouraged before continuing. /> (text-style:"fidget")[As soon as your text sends, your stomach starts grumbling. So you heat up a quick instant ramen for dinner and begin studying for your exam.] (if:$points <= -5)[[[Ultimately...|SPIRAL]]](else:)[[[Next...|phase1]]] (set: $points to it - 1) (text-style:"fidget")[Ultimately,] (text-style:"fidget")[you continue to not take care of yourself. You push your friends away, postpone plans indefinitely, and you can't remember the last time you had time for your hobbies. By working harder now, you'll stress less later you justify to yourself. But the latter never seems to happen. There's always another deadline and more responsibilities, and the weight of it all is crushing. Your friends praise how successful you are, but complain that they rarely see you anymore. You keep all your struggles to yourself.] (if:(history: where its name contains "therapy")'s length >= 1)[(text-style:"fidget")[Though you've tried therapy, you don't actively engage or apply your therapist's advice to your life. As a result, it doesn't feel like therapy works, so you are inconsistent about going and eventually quit going altogether.] ] (text-style:"fidget")[Eventually, your self-imposed isolation and lack of self-care spirals into (text-style:"blur")[emptiness and loneliness], and you begin to show signs of depression as well.] THE END. --- Anxiety and depression are closely-linked and highly comorbid. In other words, people experiencing anxiety are at a higher risk for developing depression, and vice versa. Often, anxiety manifests as pervasive worrying which may cause one to feel negatively about themselves for being unable to stop irrational nervousness and pessimism, leading to the development of depressive symptoms. Thus, self-care and help from mental health professionals are essential, not only to enforce positive coping mechanisms and build resilience to stress, but also to prevent anxiety from spiraling to combine with depression. To learn more about the relationship between anxiety and depression, check out the following links: * <a href='https://www.nami.org/Blogs/NAMI-Blog/January-2018/The-Comorbidity-of-Anxiety-and-Depression' target='_blank'>The Comorbidity of Anxiety and Depression</a> * <a href='https://www.hartgrovehospital.com/relationship-anxiety-depression/' target='_blank'>The Relationship Between Anxiety and Depression</a> * <a href='https://ajp.psychiatryonline.org/doi/10.1176/appi.ajp.2020.20030305' target='_blank'>The Critical Relationship Between Anxiety and Depression</a> If the interactive story has resonated with you, or reminds you of anyone in your life, check out the following links to learn more about types of anxiety and where to find help: * <a href='https://www.hhs.gov/answers/mental-health-and-substance-abuse/what-are-the-five-major-types-of-anxiety-disorders/index.html' target='_blank'>What Are the Five Major Types of Anxiety Disorders?</a> * <a href='https://www.verywellmind.com/what-is-high-functioning-anxiety-4140198' target='_blank'>The Characteristics of High Functioning Anxiety</a> * <a href='https://www.anxiety.org/how-to-find-a-therapist-to-treat-your-anxiety-disorder' target='_blank'>How to Find a Therapist to Treat Your Anxiety Disorder</a> * <a href='https://www.samhsa.gov/find-help/national-helpline' target='_blank'>SAMHSA'S National Mental Health Hotline</a> (text-style:"fidget")[You speculate it's probably because you just didn't drink enough water today.] (text-style:"fidget")[You try to compensate by eating a big meal and drinking lots of water because you don't want your friend to worry. But if you're being honest, you just haven't had much of an appetite recently.] (text-style:"fidget")[Afterwards, you take a nap and hope to feel better the next morning.] (if:$points <= -5)[[[Ultimately...|BURNOUT]]](else:)[[[Next...|phase1]]] (set: $points to it - 1) (text-style:"fidget")[You open up about feeling overwhelmed.] (text-style:"fidget")[As you talk, your friend listens intently, letting you rant for as long as you want while you voice out all your frustrations and worries. When you finish talking, you realize you've been feeling this way for a really long time, but until now, you have been in denial about the extent of the problem.] (if:(history: where its name contains "faint")'s length >= 1)+(text-style:"fidget")[You recognize that the cause of your fainting spell today was a panic attack.] (text-style:"fidget")[You wonder outloud if you would benefit from the help of a mental health professional, and the look of care and concern on your friend agrees.] (if:(history: where its name contains "therapy")'s length is 0)[[[Next...|begin]]](else:) [[[You decide to re-start therapy. |therapy]] ] (set: $askMore to false)(text-style:"fidget")[Ultimately, ] (text-style:"fidget")[by the end of the week, you feel good about your exam, the interview went well, and all the assignments you were stressed about are completed and turned in. You feel like all your hard work has paid off. You think things are starting to look up for you, and you expect your stress to subside.] (text-style:"rumble")[Not long after, however, there's more homework to do, another exam looming, and you're plagued with imposter syndrome about starting your new job in a few months. The stresses never quite melt away and you always feel like youre inches away from drowning.] (if:(history: where its name contains "therapy")'s length >= 1)[(text-style:"fidget")[Though you've tried therapy, you continue to believe that your stress is only conditional to a lack of success, instead of truly accepting your anxiety. As a result, you tend to quit whenever everything seems like it will be better instead of working to better yourself through the bad and the good. ] ] (text-style:"fidget")[Eventually, your swinging highs and lows lead to greater emotional exhaustion, cynicism, and a lack of self-compassion in line with symptoms of burnout.] THE END. --- Anxiety is not situational, and though it may seem like it at the time, no amount of success will ever "cure" anxiety. Instead, continuing on as is will more likely result in burnout. Burnout is a psychological syndrome that results from unmanaged, chronic workplace or academic stress characterized by emotional exhaustion, cynicism, and reduced personal accomplishment. Despite seeming successful to other people, someone experiencing burnout may not view themselves as such, and therefore never feel accomplished or a sense of self-satisfaction. There is ongoing research that suggests people who experience higher levels of anxiety are more likely to develop burnout. To learn more about burnout, and its studied relationship to anxiety, check out the following links: * <a href='https://www.who.int/news/item/28-05-2019-burn-out-an-occupational-phenomenon-international-classification-of-diseases' target='_blank'>Burn-out</a> * <a href='https://www.frontiersin.org/articles/10.3389/fpsyg.2019.00284/full' target='_blank'>The Relationship Between Burnout, Depression, and Anxiety: A Systematic Review and Meta-Analysis</a> * <a href='https://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0157013' target='_blank'>Relationship between Anxiety and Burnout among Chinese Physicians: A Moderated Mediation Model</a> If the interactive story has resonated with you, or reminds you of anyone in your life, check out the following links to learn more about types of anxiety and where to find help: * <a href='https://www.hhs.gov/answers/mental-health-and-substance-abuse/what-are-the-five-major-types-of-anxiety-disorders/index.html' target='_blank'>What Are the Five Major Types of Anxiety Disorders?</a> * <a href='https://www.verywellmind.com/what-is-high-functioning-anxiety-4140198' target='_blank'>The Characteristics of High Functioning Anxiety</a> * <a href='https://www.anxiety.org/how-to-find-a-therapist-to-treat-your-anxiety-disorder' target='_blank'>How to Find a Therapist to Treat Your Anxiety Disorder</a> * <a href='https://www.samhsa.gov/find-help/national-helpline' target='_blank'>SAMHSA'S National Mental Health Hotline</a> (text-style:"fidget")[You begin therapy with a determined mindset , telling yourself that it's only precautionary to prevent yourself from spiraling into actually anxiety.] (text-style:"fidget")[While you wait your turn in the waiting room of the counseling office, you try your best to shake a sense of shame and nervousness. THE END. --- Vulnerability and self-reflection are key to acknowledging a desire for better mental health. To take next steps, mental health professionals are best equipped to not only listen to your concerns and stresses, but also enlighten you on how to recognize negative avoidance behaviors, introduce positive coping strategies, and foster a healthier perspective and state of mind to build resilience against the stresses of everyday life. She suggests something you can try next time is to close your eyes to decrease simulation. Then, focus your attention to the noises and sounds of your surroundings, including maybe the sound of footsteps of strangers walking past you, or the wind in the trees, or maybe the clicking of your roommate's keyboard...until eventually, your mind stops fixating on your stressors, and is instead distracted by the noises around you. [[Next...|therapy]] (set: $points to it + 1) (set: $askMore to true)(text-style:"fidget")[You thank your therapist for her time and the talk.] (text-style:"fidget")[Your therapist reminds you to try to incorporate her tips and find time for self-reflection until your next appointment. ] (if:$studyNext is true)[[[Next...|study]]](else:)[[Next...|panic]] (set: $askMore to false)(text-style:"fidget")[Your therapist points out that you have a tendency to fall for common thought traps for people who experience anxiety. Also known as cognitive distortions, these thinking patterns are exaggerated or irrational, which contribute to a greater sense of stress and danger than may be necessary. She gives you the following list of thought traps: ] {(text-style:"fidget")[* generalization: taking one isolated negative incident and believing it to be a never-ending pattern of loss and defeat] (text-style:"fidget")[* discounting the positive/mental filter: dismissing successes, fixating on failures] (text-style:"fidget")[* catastrophizing: assuming the worst in every scenario] (text-style:"fidget")[* emotional reasoning: interpreting the way you feel as a matter of fact //(e.g. "I feel like everyone hates me, so they must hate me")//] (text-style:"fidget")[* personalization: blaming yourself completely for situations you had no or only partial control over] (text-style:"fidget")[* control fallacies: feeling like you are responsible for everything or have no control at all in your life]} (text-style:"fidget")[As she briefly describes each cognitive distortion, you realize how many of these you follow so naturally.] (text-style:"fidget")[She explains that there are many other distortions as well, and the importance of recognizing or fall into these logical traps, and adjusting or mentality whenever we do so.] [[Next...|tips]] --- <a href='https://www.verywellmind.com/cognitive-distortions-and-anxiety-1393157' target='_blank'>Cognitive Distortions in Generalized Anxiety Disorder</a>
